Wow.. they found a 152 and 164 to join the show. Only 1 person in a 100k has an IQ of 164 or higher. So there are only 680 people in all of UK with an IQ equal or higher than that lady. That's insane.
I would like to say be wary of IQ tests as they do not account for certain aspects of intelligence. Many tests exclude sciences, emotional/psychological intelligence among other things. Many are also culturally exclusive. To label someone smart or dumb based on a narrow range of testing is "stupid" to say the least. For instance, if you took someone from a tribe in the amazon and gave a standardized IQ test you may label them "borderline" intelligence comparatively. However, if you tested their ability to solve problems in the amazon compared to a city person they will likely be a genius and may consider the city dweller "borderline" by their standards. A politician may be terrible in math and vocabulary but a master emotional manipulator, and maybe had to develop that intelligence in navigating a very different reality/lifestyle than someone else. Point being, there are different facets to intelligence so do not put too much faith in an IQ test.

There is zero chance she is 164 IQ. You would never get that number from professional psychometric testing, and not be able to do 2 digit arithmetic math. The real psychometric tests take mental processing speed into account since you're on a timer, the questions get brutal the further along you go on the lists they use. You can be a genius but bad at math, for example Richard Feynman the famous physicist had 125 IQ, but you get tested on multiple areas and critera, if you're some spatial processing and pattern recognition prodigy, but still really bad at math, it's still going to be impossible to get above 140 IQ.

I doubt that the model has an IQ of 70 if 100 is the mean and if 15 is the standarddeviation. Because when 100 is the mean and when 15 is the standarddeviation, then a test result of 70 to 79 is close to be mentally handicapped while a result below 70 is equivalent to be mentally handicapped. And I don't think the model was handicapped. Also the questions in this video were not all testing cognitive intelligence, but knowledge.
An absolute number alone means nothing, if you don't know the mean and the standarddeviation. I think of IQ as a test result (which can vary for the same person depending on if the person had a good day or a bad day) and I think of IQ as a percentage X meaning "A person with an IQ of X % has a better result than X % of all the people who took the test". This way you can summarize the test result of a person as one, single (relative) number.

Shakespeare did not die the same day he was born. The story, that he died the same day as he was born was made by people of the times as this gave his life itself a deeper meaning / purpose and added more 'flavour' to him as a person. Even today we adore stories and books starting and ending in the same way. It has smth magical to it.   In Shakespeare's case, this story gave more value to his projects as his name truly became a brand and made him more well known. All thanks to that sort of ending. Obviously it also made people (who sold his stuff or advertised for it) gain more money, too. In the end, even today, we still wonder if he truly wrote all of his plays. Many are confirmed, but others do not quite fit his style of writing. His true birth date is also unknown. I have read different articles... and they all state different dates, while also bringing up his alleged same death day. The death date is well recorded, but the birthday is unknown.   In the end Shakespear is shrouded in mystery to some degree and I prefer it stay that way, as this makes it way more fun to analyse and think about.

My IQ is 148, actually Mensa tested in Belfast, Northern Ireland â€” in English, while my native language is not English. But I'm single, mediocre job, don't own a car, don't have many friends. So it doesn't guarantee you will succeed in life. In fact I am plagued with anxieties, paranoia (mainly about getting fired) & insomnia (I can literally not stop thinking until I am dead tired), and sleep only 4 hours per night. I do always win in Trivia games, speak 4 languages (in which I can do business presentations, and even tutor those languages to the natives speakers), knew that the next number (@00:11:20 in the sequence 121, 144, 169, 196...) was 225 in less than 1 second, I was able to read at age 4, and able to calculate by heart in fractions (1/4 times 2/3 divided by 1/2 etc.) at age 5. I am certainly book smart, pick up a new skill (like programming, designing spread sheets in a few days) and can memorise things easily. Like I know all James Bond film titles in chronological order, and can name you all the 50 American States alphabetically, among other things. But as I said, it is not a guarantee for success.  My best mate has an IQ of 90 and has his own brewery, a wife and a kid.  A nice trivia for you: average IQ in any country is always 100. But the 100 IQ point is measurably different between countries. Anything between 85-115 is normal, most people are in that bracket. But for every person with an IQ of 150, there is a person with an IQ of 50. How it is calculated, in percentiles, it means 100 is the exact mathematical average. Saying an IQ of 105 is the average is like saying 5 degrees Celsius is the freezing/thawing point of fresh water.   People around 70 or lower are effectively less functional, but even that does not guarantee things. I have a neighbor, with an IQ of about 65, and she is happily married to a guy with a successful butcher shop, and 4 daughters. According to ChatGPT 3.5:  IQ scores are typically categorized into various ranges to help interpret an individual's cognitive abilities. These categories can vary depending on the specific IQ test and the organization using them, but here are some common categories:  Mental Retardation (Intellectual Disability): IQ below 70-75 (approximately) This category is often subdivided into different levels of intellectual disability, including mild, moderate, severe, and profound.  Borderline Intellectual Functioning (BIF): IQ range of 70-85 (approximately) Individuals in this range may have some difficulties with cognitive tasks but often function reasonably well in daily life.  Below Average: IQ range of 86-99 (approximately) Individuals in this range may have average to below-average cognitive abilities.  Average: IQ range of 100-115 (approximately) This is the average range, where most people's IQ scores fall.  Above Average: IQ range of 116-130 (approximately) Individuals in this range are often considered to have above-average cognitive abilities. Gifted:  IQ above 130 (approximately) Gifted individuals are considered to have exceptionally high cognitive abilities.  It's important to note that these categories are not universally agreed upon, and different IQ tests and institutions may use slightly different ranges or terminology. Additionally, IQ scores are just one measure of cognitive abilities and should be interpreted alongside other factors when assessing an individual's capabilities. Furthermore, the interpretation of IQ scores can vary depending on the purpose of the assessment, such as clinical diagnosis, educational placement, or employment screening.

(accurately) measuring IQ over 135 becomes highly unreliable anyway. I'm sure she's above 135, but I would take anything over 135 with a grain of salt - not to downplay their intelligence, but because there's really no need to measure any further than that anyways and as such most modern tools (read: tests , because there really is no other way to measure) are not suited to _accurately_ measure (above) that level of intelligence..  Anything over 135 is considered highly gifted and you're already in the 1% top.  The vast vast majority of people also massively overestimate their IQ by a considerable margin because they base their scores on silly online tests. If you get an IQ of 120 on a random online test then i have bad news for you. Do/ purchase an actual WAIS-IV test to start with if you want to measure your intelligence somewhat reliably.  Lastly, all these 'general knowledge' questions do very little to measure actual intellect.

"According to Psychologists, there are four types of Intelligence:   1) Intelligence Quotient (IQ) 2) Emotional Quotient (EQ) 3) Social Quotient (SQ) 4) Adversity Quotient (AQ)  1. Intelligence Quotient (IQ): this is the measure of your level of comprehension. You need IQ to solve maths, memorize things, and recall lessons.  2. Emotional Quotient (EQ): this is the measure of your ability to maintain peace with others, keep to time, be responsible, be honest, respect boundaries, be humble, genuine and considerate.  3. Social Quotient (SQ): this is the measure of your ability to build a network of friends and maintain it over a long period of time.  People that have higher EQ and SQ tend to go further in life than those with a high IQ but low EQ and SQ. Most schools capitalize on improving IQ levels while EQ and SQ are played down.  A man of high IQ can end up being employed by a man of high EQ and SQ even though he has an average IQ.  Your EQ represents your Character, while your SQ represents your Charisma. Give in to habits that will improve these three Qs, especially your EQ and SQ.  Now there is a 4th one, a new paradigm:  4. The Adversity Quotient (AQ): The measure of your ability to go through a rough patch in life, and come out of it without losing your mind.  When faced with troubles, AQ determines who will give up, who will abandon their family, and who will consider suicide.  Parents please expose your children to other areas of life than just Academics. They should adore manual labour (never use work as a form of punishment), Sports and Arts.  Develop their IQ, as well as their EQ, SQ and AQ. They should become multifaceted human beings able to do things independently of their parents, teachers & coaches.

According to some research, an IQ score exceeding 145 is only found in 0.003% of the population. That's 3 out 100,000 people.  Now a score of 164 is a little bit more rare than "just" 145+. On a 16 SD scale (such as the Stanford-Binet test), an IQ score of 164 is at the 99.9999980964% percentile, which means that only 0.0000019036% of people have this score or higher. This translates to a rarity of 1 in 52,530,944 people.  It's still important to understand that these percentage values are not absolute despite their apparent accuracy. Different tests provide different scores and estimates. For example, according to the IQ percentile calculator, an IQ score of 164 on a 15 SD scale (such as the Wechsler tests) is at the 99.9999999968% percentile, which means that only 0.0000000032% of people have this score or higher. This would translate to a rarity of 1 in 30,938,221,975 people. This estimate obviously differs drastically from the Stanford-Binet estimate above, meaning it's difficult to actually draw any deeply meaningful data out of them... Well, we can confidently deduce is that Abby performs exceptionally well in IQ tests, but not much beyond that.
